    "in 2002 , e.kuwert and r.schtzle considered in their work _ gradient flow for the willmore functional  @xcite two - dimensional compact immersed surfaces @xmath1 in @xmath2 moving by the gradient of the willmore functional @xmath3 , that is , solutions of @xmath4 with @xmath5 called willmore flow . here , @xmath6 is the trace - free part of the second fundamental form and @xmath7 is the induced area measure on @xmath1 .",
    "the authors gave a lower bound on the lifespan of a smooth solution , which depends only on how much the curvature of the initial surface is concentrated in space .",
    "moreover , they showed that the curvature concentrates in space if a finite time singularity develops . in a second joint work",
    "@xcite kuwert and schtzle continued studying those singularities in greater detail by setting up a blow - up procedure .",
    "more precisely , they proved apart from other results that a suitable blow - up converges to a nonumbilic willmore surface . in his lecture",
    "notes @xcite , not only gave a broad summary of the above subjects and other works , but also performed a somewhat refined analysis concerning the behaviour of the flow near an assumed singularity .",
    "+ the aim of this thesis is , roughly speaking , to generalize @xcite , the blow - up procedure in @xcite and parts of @xcite in the sense that we study the willmore functional and the corresponding willmore flow on riemannian manifolds @xmath8 of bounded geometry as the target .",
    "that is , manifolds with @xmath9 bounds on the riemannian curvature tensor and with a strictly positive injectivity radius .",
    "we denote by @xmath10 and @xmath11 the mean curvature vector and second fundamental form respectively . in @xmath2 with the standard metric tensor the respective gradient flows of the functionals induced by the energies @xmath12 @xmath13 and @xmath14 are all equivalent since they differ only by a topological constant .",
    "this is in general no longer true for non - flat targets as it is described in section [ wfdef ] in detail .",
    "we decided to study @xmath15 that is , the flow @xmath16 where the @xmath0 gradient refers to the metric tensor @xmath17 on @xmath18 .",
    "+ in the first chapter we give a detailed overview of the notation used in this work . in particular , we adopted the so - called star notation @xmath19 for tensors @xmath11 and @xmath20 used for example in @xcite , @xcite and @xcite to describe nonlinearities in the evolution equations to be developed . in our setting of a non - flat ambient manifold it is suitable to extend such a notation for terms involving the riemannian curvature tensor as it was used in @xcite for the study of the evolution of elastic curves in riemannian manifolds .",
    "later on , we collect basic facts such as classical differential geometric identities as well as variational formulas for various geometric objects as in @xcite . +   + analogously to the approach in @xcite we prove a lower bound for the maximal time span of smooth existence of the flow .",
    "chapter two establishes this lower bound in four steps : first , we compute the evolution of derivatives of the curvature @xmath21 where @xmath22 denotes a universal sum of terms depending multilinearly on derivatives of the curvature ( see proposition 2.4 , @xcite ) . the @xmath23-terms basically denote universal sums of terms depending multilinearly on derivatives of the curvature and the riemannian curvature tensor @xmath24 the precise algebraic structure is not being used here .",
    "second , this information will then be transformed into localized @xmath0-type integral estimates ( cf .",
    "[ lemma34 ] ) .",
    "to further estimate the right hand side , i.e. the nonlinearities in ( [ eveq ] ) , we use interpolation and absorption techniques . to do so , it is essential to assume that the concentration of the curvature is locally small .",
    "third , to interpolate the higher nonlinearities we need to generalize a sobolev inequality originally due to michael and simon @xcite for the case @xmath25 up to a little worsening , we prove a generalization of the aforementioned sobolev inequality for isometrically immersed manifolds of any codimension provided the ricci tensor of @xmath8 is bounded in @xmath26 and the injectivity radius is strictly positive ( see [ mssi ] ) . in a last step , we employ a multiplicative sobolev inequality , which is likewise based on the sobolev inequality above , to obtain interior @xmath9-estimates for the curvature still assuming small curvature concentration ( see [ prop47 ] ) .",
    "controlling the growth of the maximal local curvature concentration then allows us to bound from below the first time this smallness condition is violated .",
    "+   + to state the main theorem of chapter two , that is , the lifespan estimate , we want to introduce some preliminary definitions .",
    "first , we want to define the following non - local quantity used to control the maximal local energy concentration .",

    "numerical examples of mayer and simonett @xcite indicate the existence of finite time singularities in euclidean space . in the same geometric setting blatt @xcite",
    "has shown analytically that singularities may occur at finite or infinite time . however , to our knowledge there is no analytical evidence for the existence of finite time singularities . as has been done in @xcite and @xcite , we perform a blow - up procedure at an assumed singularity . using the result of the lifespan estimate",
    "we show that the rescaled flows ( sub-)converge to a static willmore surface , that is , a static critical point of @xmath61 for this , we use a compactness theorem that goes back to langer @xcite and has then been generalized by breuning @xcite .",
    "it turns out to be an essential assumption that the area is uniformly bounded along the flow .",
    "namely , to obtain compactness there are basically two conditions to be fulfilled .",
    "first , the curvature has to be bounded in @xmath9 and second , a mass - density estimate has to be obeyed . to satisfy the first condition",
    ", we prove a second version of interior @xmath9-estimates for the curvature similar to those of kuwert and schtzle @xcite using a localization in time ( see [ interiorestimates ] ) .",
    "the second version allows to perform a blow - up at an assumed singularity at infinity because the first version ( see [ prop47 ] ) depends on initial curvature estimates in contrast to the second depending on uniform area estimates .",
    "the latter dependence is due to an extra area term in the above mentioned @xmath0-estimates calculated in the second chapter ( cf . also the remark on page ) . to satisfy the second condition of the above compactness theorem we establish a mass - density estimate for immersed surfaces in manifolds of bounded geometry of order one , at least for radii that are small enough depending on the geometry of the ambient space . for large radii",
    "we were again forced to make the assumption that the area is bounded so that the large scale estimate is then trivially fulfilled .",
    "+   + we now want to formulate the main theorem of the third chapter .",
    "to prove this theorem , a building block is to make the assumption that for a maximal willmore flow the total area is uniformly bounded by a number @xmath62 as mentioned above . fortunately , this requirement is satisfied for finite singularities and for ambient manifolds of strictly negative curvature ( see the remark below [ blowupthm ] ) .",

    "<S> we consider the @xmath0 gradient flow for the willmore functional in riemannian manifolds of bounded geometry . in the euclidean case e.kuwert and r.schtzle [ _ gradient flow for the willmore functional , _ comm . </S>",

    "<S> , 10 : 307 - 339 , 2002 ] established a lower bound of a smooth solution of such a flow , which depends only on how much the curvature of the initial surface is concentrated in space . in a second joint work [ _ the willmore flow with small initial energy , _ j.differential geom . , 57 : 409 - 441 , 2001 ] the aforementioned authors proved that a suitable blow - up converges to a nonumbilic ( compact or noncompact ) willmore surface . in the lecture notes of the first author [ _ </S>",
    "<S> the willmore functional , _ unpublished lecture notes , eth zrich , 2007 ] the blow - up analysis was refined . in the present work </S>",
    "<S> we intend to generalize the results mentioned above to the riemannian setting .    [ [ section ] ] </S>"
